That setting seemed appropriate for Ron Adams, the Warriors\u2019 defensive guru and one of the NBA\u2019s most thoughtful interview subjects. Adams, 71, is a wholistic coach, a native Californian whose career instructing and imparting wisdom to players dates to 1969, when he started as an assistant at Fresno Pacific University (his alma mater). His theories and concepts have been honed through stops at Fresno State and, starting in 1992, in the NBA at San Antonio, Philadelphia, Milwaukee, Chicago, Oklahoma City, Boston and now Golden State. During his time as an assistant, Adams\u2019 teams have reached the postseason 17 times, including four Finals and three championships in his time with Golden State.  Adams joined the Warriors in 2014 as much to mentor then-new coach Steve Kerr as to shape their defense. It was a merging of old school and new age that both men swiftly embraced. NBA.com\u2019s Steve Aschburner spoke with the veteran coach after the team\u2019s practice in Cambridge. * * * Steve Aschburner:  So much attention has been paid to DeMarcus Cousins\u2019 addition to your lineup, as far as giving you five dangerous scorers and no one that opponents comfortably can leave to double-team elsewhere. But I\u2019m eager to learn about Cousins as a defender and what your team and he are facing on that side of the ball. Ron Adams:  There are some challenges. One of them is, he hasn\u2019t played for a year, regardless of any of the skills you\u2019re looking at. But we kind of anticipated what we thought he could do and build a system that works for him. Having said that, I\u2019ve been pleased with his defense in the four games that he\u2019s played. He gives us a different look in the paint, obviously, but he\u2019s a quick player. He\u2019s got good feet. I don\u2019t think defense has always been upper-most in his mind in the past. But he\u2019s been quite good thus far. He\u2019s shown that he anticipates well and reads well. We do quite a bit of switching \u2014 he\u2019s done a little bit of that lately, and he\u2019s pretty good at it. But we\u2019re trying to bring that aspect along with him. I think he\u2019s shown good awareness and he\u2019s played with good spirit, and really has been a pleasure to be around. SA:  You mention quick feet, but this is a guy recovering from Achilles tendon surgery. RA:  If you look at DeMarcus\u2019 career, and he\u2019d tell you this too, he\u2019s been pretty oriented toward offense, toward rebounding the ball and defending in the paint. But he does have good feet \u2014 I don\u2019t think the injury has hurt him at all. In fact, that Achilles is a lot stronger than the other one, I\u2019m sure now. These rehabs are really intense and he put a lot of good work into it. It\u2019s more of a mentality with him. I think he\u2019s bought in well. He wants to do well. And he\u2019s shown good focus on the defensive end. SA:  How much does it help that he\u2019s with a team that demands defense and has proven the value of it? As opposed to Cousins\u2019 exuberance over this opportunity and wanting to be a good employee who doesn\u2019t rock the boat? RA:  It\u2019s a little bit of everything you\u2019ve mentioned. But he\u2019s a good basketball guy. He likes the game. He wants to get better. Certainly, the emphasis of the team has helped him, as far as wanting to be balanced offensively and defensively. If you want to win championships and you\u2019re not playing great defense, that\u2019s not going to happen for you. But I\u2019ve found him very open to what we\u2019ve had to say. I see him working on things that are important to our program. I think he\u2019s internalized those things so they\u2019re important to him. SA:  What role do the other players play in this, on court and off, in blending him into the team\u2019s culture? RA:  Certainly the nature of our group has helped him. Our guys were so supportive of him after the first game, it was really gratifying to watch the response of our team. They want him to do well, as do our coaches. This might be a very short stay here, who knows? But to a man on our coaching staff, and Steve [Kerr] is so great at this, we really want him to get back on his feet and be the player he was \u2014 and some. I think he understands that about us. Steve is so inclusive and so helpful to a player like DeMarcus. So we\u2019re making progress. It\u2019s going to be a while. He\u2019s really helped us offensively already \u2014 he\u2019s a great passer, he\u2019s been a good quarterback for us too. The other part of his game is growing.  SA:  Do you anticipate he\u2019s going to be attacked on pick-and-rolls? He has been a target for that in the past. RA:  Teams had their strategies. But I don\u2019t see that being a huge problem. In the orthodox coverages of the game I think he\u2019s fine. In the new age, when people are coming off shooting threes and that pick is set at the 3-point line, that\u2019s when you have to make some adjustments. I think he\u2019s shown already he\u2019ll be capable of doing that. SA:  You\u2019ve mentioned Steve, a guy you have been mentoring as a coach. Five seasons in, what are your impressions? RA:  What you would expect just from the technical standpoint. He\u2019s become a very good coach on both sides of the ball, and he really enjoys it. Keeps growing in that regard, which is to be expected. Steve is a very bright guy, knows the game well before becoming a coach. He\u2019s such a measured person in how he looks at the game \u2014 he\u2019s a very competitive guy \u2014 and what his long view is. I mean, we all get better. I\u2019m 71 years old and I\u2019m learning every year. This league \u2026 even this year from last year, there\u2019s changes in how the game is played. The mentality. Now we\u2019re into a \u201cnot practice too much, make sure your guys are healthy\u201d phase. It\u2019s much more of an emphasis now. So you have stark changes and a lot of subtle ones. Steve\u2019s philosophy for how a team should operate is, I think, spot-on for the modern age. And I think this has been helpful for DeMarcus, by the way. We don\u2019t want him changing his style as a player, but we do hope, as with all of our guys, that they play the game with joy. Enjoy themselves, enjoy each other, stay mindful of how fortunate they are.  SA:  As a defensive-focused coach, you\u2019ve been around from the days of hand-checking and intensely physical play to this new era of \u201cfreedom of movement\u201d in which defenders dare not even breathe on an opponent. RA:  This year\u2019s been a little frustrating at times. It just means you have to do certain things better. One thing is defensive transition, and even when you transition well, so many people are shooting early threes. We have teams with five 3-point shooters in their lineups and it\u2019s putting a lot of stress on defensive transition. Your team aspects, your help aspects have to be good. How you handle the kinds of penetrations that the new rules are allowing for more. Seemingly the offensive player can do little wrong. We\u2019ve got a lot of pushing off offensively on guys, which seems to be OK at the moment, perhaps until the playoffs come, I don\u2019t know. These changes, you can adjust to them through your help-side defense, your cell, the kinds of things every team teaches. But when something is taken away from you in a system, you have to put more emphasis on team play. SA:  Do you ever feel picked on, which so many changes favoring offense? RA:  I don\u2019t feel picked on. I look at it as a challenge. It has its frustrations. But I think when all is said and done, the good defensive teams will be there at the end. Whatever the definition of that is. You adjust. The NBA is so fascinating \u2014 there are so many facets to it. \u2026 It taxes one but it also broadens one. SA:  You long have been a devotee of switching on defense, to maintain maximum pressure on the ball. Now so many teams do that \u2014 is it gratifying to see them adopt your methods? RA:  When a team is winning and does something, everyone looks at it. You look at the roster and say, \u201cWell, maybe we should build our roster like Team A has.\u201d I must say, some teams have emulated us and emulated us very well, because they\u2019re very tough. [laughs] And they\u2019re loaded with great depth and do things so well. SA:  Can you compare the Warriors\u2019 defense from one year to the next? Or even rank them? Maybe it\u2019s like ranking your kids. Or maybe the rules and personnel changes make that difficult. RA:  No, I can make some comparisons. We have been kind of up and down. Statistically, we\u2019re a middle-of-the-pack team right now. Some stats are good, others aren\u2019t. I\u2019d like our field-goal defensive percentage to be a little better and our 3-point defensive percentage to be better. Early in the year, I think we were tops in 3-point defense. We kind of play up and down in the regular season. But seldom do we not get the other team\u2019s best game. Statistically, I allow for that. [Saturday] was a huge game for Boston \u2014 you get people\u2019s best. When we let down, and it can be any team \u2026 Phoenix does not have a glossy record but they have talent and they\u2019re tough to play. If we\u2019re not ready on that given night, the evening can get long. That\u2019s the fun thing about being a champion, that\u2019s the thing you have to embrace and recognize. Steve goes a masterful job of understanding this. Working around it and not getting too distraught when things aren\u2019t picture-perfect on the court. He helps me in that regard. SA:  So which edition of the Warriors was your best defensive team? RA:  I would say the first three teams were awfully, awfully good. Probably with more consistency in the regular season. But with us, we look at what we do when the second season starts. And we\u2019ve been sterling. That\u2019s the confidence that we have. When the playoffs start, we really start focusing on our opponent and feel good about what the defense will do on any given game. That\u2019s been pretty much the story the last four years. Last year\u2019s team, when it came down to it, in certain moments was every bit as good as those other teams. SA:  You\u2019re talking experience, muscle memory, confidence? RA: We all know what we can do when we\u2019re focused. When those times come in a game when we\u2019re not as focused as we\u2019d like, in a traditional coaching sense, we kind of understand our team. And again, Steve is so good in having foresight and believing in this team. SA:  Are you guys able to weigh the cumulative wear and tear of four extra-long seasons, going on five, against the accumulated knowledge and confidence of successfully handling it all? RA:  Once you win a championship, it changes your perspective \u2014 I\u2019m talking about players. It\u2019s not easy, very difficult to achieve, but the confidence that comes with it serves you well in critical periods of the games. SA:  So how are your players holding up from 100-plus games year after year? RA:  I keep going back to this, but Steve\u2019s done a good job with that. Sometimes when our performance is up and down, there\u2019s an understanding of that. It\u2019s not college. You\u2019re not going to beat your guys up in practice, but you want to be efficient. You want to stay organized. You want to reinforce all the good habits that allow us to do what we do. But there has to be a good formula with the end, the playoffs, being the thing you\u2019re tailoring everything around. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Happy Monday, everyone."},{"id":36055,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/about-last-night-1-26-19","date":"2019-01-27","title":"About Last Night: Kerr obliterates coaching record","content":" During this Warriors dynasty, KD and Steph and Klay and Draymond have us accustomed to the unprecedented, to the previously unfathomable expansion of options for that which can simply *be* during a basketball game. That\u2019s why it\u2019s important to acknowledge another moment in the league-wide, pace-and-space mayhem: On Saturday, Steve Kerr, the coach overseeing Golden State\u2019s championship ascent, won regular-season game No. 300 on the road in Boston. He has been coach for 377 games. Less than five seasons. Let that simmer. It took previous record-holder Pat Riley \u2013 an NBA legend and bag-full-of-rings champion as a player, coach and executive \u2013 415 games. Half an NBA campaign behind! With the Showtime Lakers! In fact, Kerr is the fastest to reach 300 victories in any of the nation\u2019s major sports leagues, beating out MLB\u2019s Frank Chance (426), the NFL\u2019s Don Shula (442) and NHL coach Bruce Coubdreau (496). (No MLS coach has yet achieved the feat.) This is a thing, what Kerr has accomplished. None of this is to say Boston made this easy. The Celtics pushed the Warriors throughout, with Kyrie turning in a 32-6-10, Al Horford adding 22-13-3 and Marcus Smart nailing a tying 3 within the final minute of regulation. Surely someone would have eventually noticed the considerable skills of Morant. The 6-foot-3 sophomore guard \u2014 who\u2019s now stars for Murray State \u2014 leads the nation in assists per game (10.7) by a huge margin. He\u2019s averaging 24.1 points and almost 5.8 rebounds per game, blowing up YouTube with an eye-popping array of acrobatic dunks, all while being seriously considered as both a national player of the year candidate and an NBA lottery pick. Back in 2016, Morant was just another overlooked prospect who lived in the country (Dalzell, S.C.), didn\u2019t play for an AAU team backed by a major shoe company and didn\u2019t even use social media. He was a textbook example of a sleeper \u2014 until Kane asked someone at the combine where the concession stand was. On his way there, he heard a basketball bouncing in a side gym, far from the main action. Curious, he looked inside. There Kane first laid eyes on Morant, who was playing in a game of three-on-three. After watching for five minutes, during which Morant\u2019s 44-inch vertical leap, quickness and uncanny passing eye were on full display, Kane forgot about his hunger pangs and dashed off to call Murray State coach Matt McMahon. \u201cHe said, \u2018this kid\u2019s gonna be a pro,\u2019 \u201d McMahon says. \u201cSo I jumped in the car and got up there the next day. We tracked him all through July.\u201d Murray State\u2019s coaches quickly built a relationship with Morant\u2019s close-knit family and then sat back and hoped no other recruiters would notice what Kane saw. By the end of July, Morant committed to Murray State, intrigued by the possibility of following former Racer point guards Isaiah Canaan and Cameron Payne \u2014 both of whom made it to the NBA \u2014 and playing alongside senior Jonathan Stark, who had averaged 22 points and six assists as a junior. Only after announcing his decision did Morant start getting flooded with offers, but by then it was too late. \u201cI decided to set official visits to Murray State and South Carolina,\u201d Morant says. \u201cBut once I went to Murray, I knew that\u2019s where I needed to be. The point guard tradition played a part, but not as much as the community \u2014 I felt like everybody, from the players to the coaches to the fans, were like a family. I\u2019m a big family guy. Everybody in the community loves the team.\u201d Another lure was Murray State\u2019s up-tempo offense, which gives breathing room to point guards with the talent to make plays. Morant fits in perfectly, and although his turnover rate is high, McMahon isn\u2019t about to shackle him. \u201cI want him to play with all the creativity and freedom and confidence he can,\u201d McMahon says. \u201c[In games from Jan. 17-24] he made 11 turnovers, but he had 32 assists. That\u2019s a 3-1 assist-to-turnover ratio. I\u2019ll take that any day of the week.\u201d Morant\u2019s assists are of the spectacular variety, like the half-court, one-handed lob for a dunk he threw to Brion Sanchious for a dunk in a recent game against Belmont. Thirty-three NBA scouts were there, and though Morant turned an ankle early in the game, in his diminished state he still delivered 20 points and nine assists . Those scouts already know what Morant can do when he\u2019s healthy. He\u2019s racked up a collection of impressive performances this season, leaving opposing coaches search for the right comparison. After Morant torched Alabama for 38 points, nine rebounds and five assists , Crimson Tide coach and former NBA point guard Avery Johnson reached back into his past. \u201cI saw flashbacks of a lot of guys I played against,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cWhether it\u2019s the old Isaiah Thomas \u2014 the Detroit Pistons\u2019 Isaiah Thomas \u2014 that craftiness and cleverness. John Stockton\u2019s passing ability. Russell Westbrook\u2019s athletic ability. My God. When I saw him on film \u2026 to watch him play in person \u2026 it was better than on film. We gave him about five or six different looks. Sometimes it worked, sometimes it didn\u2019t.\u201d Missouri State coach Dana Ford saw plenty of Murray State when he was coach at Tennessee State. That didn\u2019t stop him from scheduling the Racers in his first season in Springfield. Morant delivered a 29-point, 13-rebound, 12-assist triple-double . \u201cI coached against all three [Canaan, Payne, Morant],\u201d Ford says. \u201cHe is by far the best NBA prospect of the three. He is so fast and athletic \u2026 a blur. He is a Kansas type of guard \u2026 long [limbed] and competitive. He sees the play before it develops. He\u2019s turnover prone, but that\u2019s correctable. He\u2019s a little bit of John Wall mixed with Chris Paul. He\u2019s special.\u201d Middle Tennessee coach Nick McDevitt sees traits of Westbrook in Morant, fitting because the Thunder\u2019s triple-double machine is Morant\u2019s hero. Morant didn\u2019t produce great numbers (nine points, seven assists, three rebounds) in a 64-42 win over MTSU \u2014 he didn\u2019t need to \u2014 but McDevitt saw plenty, on the court and in film scouting before the game. \u201cHe has speed, and you can\u2019t teach that,\u201d McDevitt says. \u201cCertain guys are a one-man fast break that can turn negative numbers into positive numbers for your team in a hurry. That always puts pressure on the defense. At this level anyway, it keeps you from being very aggressive on the offensive glass, because once they get it, and once he gets it, he will run by everybody you have. \u201cThat\u2019s what Westbrook figured out a long time ago. Just go get the ball. Get a defensive rebound and outrun everybody. Some guys, like Ty Lawson, he had that speed, but he couldn\u2019t go get the ball. Somebody else had to get it for him. Guys like Westbrook, and Morant \u2014 which he\u2019s shown he can do at this level \u2014 Morant can go get it himself and then he\u2019s gone. If you don\u2019t have guys back, he\u2019s gonna go shoot layups.\u201d Or more often dunks that must be watched repeatedly to be believed , like the one Morant pulled off against UT Martin earlier this month. Morant, in the left corner, snuck back door on his defender and received a perfect bounce pass from Tevin Brown as the Racers\u2019 6-foot-8 Quinton Dove moved in front to take the charge. Morant took one step, then another and launched himself over Dove for a two-handed slam . Stunning doesn\u2019t begin to describe it. Scary \u2026 that\u2019s the word. \u201cYou think you\u2019ve seen it all, and then he does something like that,\u201d McMahon said. \u201cI turned and looked into the stands and people were running up and down the aisles. The noise after the dunk was deafening. I saw a lot of shocked looks. Fortunately, there were some great camera people there in the right place at the right time.\u201d Morant laughs at the recollection. To the man who spent hours training with his father \u2014 often repeatedly jumping on top of old tires from an 18-wheeler \u2014 that dunk was just what he does. \u201cI saw the defender move over to try and take the charge,\u201d Morant says. \u201cMy mindset was just go finish the play.\u201d Morant gets a charge out of moments like that, but his favorite play in basketball is the assist. \u201cI love making my teammates\u2019 jobs easier,\u201d Morant says, \u201cputting them in spots where they can score. Just to see them with smiles on their faces, giving them confidence \u2014 that makes me feel much better than scoring the ball.\u201d McMahon has coached Morant for two seasons and never ceases to be amazed. But not necessarily by Morant\u2019s physical gifts. \u201cEveryone talks about his freakish athleticism, his explosiveness, his change of speed,\u201d McMahon says. \u201cThat\u2019s all very accurate. He\u2019s elite in those categories. But now you combine that with a guy who has an unbelievable IQ, feel for the game and vision. To me, he\u2019s a basketball genius. Now you combine that with high character and work ethic. He\u2019s all about the team and making everyone around him better. \u201cThose are the ingredients of a once-in-a-lifetime player. And that\u2019s what Ja is.\u201d * * * Chris Dortch is the editor of the Blue Ribbon College Basketball Yearbook . As the All-Star starters who led their respective conferences in fan votes during NBA All-Star Voting 2019 presented by Google, James and Antetokounmpo will serve as team captains and draft the All-Star Game rosters from the pool of players voted as starters and reserves in each conference. * View Full Results The captains will draft the eight remaining players from the starter pool in the First Round and then all 14 players from the reserve pool in the Second Round, making selections without regard to a player\u2019s conference affiliation or position. The team rosters for the 68th NBA All-Star Game will be revealed on TNT in a special NBA All-Star Draft Show on Thursday, Feb. 7 at 7 p.m. ET. The 2019 NBA All-Star Game, featuring Team LeBron vs. Team Giannis , will take place on Sunday, Feb. 17 at 8 p.m. ET at Spectrum Center in Charlotte, N.C. TNT and ESPN Radio will air the game live in the United States. NBA All-Star 2019 will reach fans in more than 200 countries and territories in more than 40 languages. * NBA All-Star 2019 full coverage James has been named an NBA All-Star for the 15th time, tied for the third-most selections in league history behind Kareem Abdul-Jabbar (19) and Kobe Bryant (18). Along with James, the Western Conference starter pool includes the Golden State Warriors\u2019 Stephen Curry (guard) and Kevin Durant (frontcourt), the Oklahoma City Thunder\u2019s Paul George (frontcourt) and the Houston Rockets\u2019 James Harden (guard). In the Eastern Conference, Antetokounmpo (frontcourt) is joined in the starter pool by the Philadelphia 76ers\u2019 Joel Embiid (frontcourt), the Boston Celtics\u2019 Kyrie Irving (guard), the Toronto Raptors\u2019 Kawhi Leonard (frontcourt) and the Charlotte Hornets\u2019 Kemba Walker (guard). This marks the first NBA All-Star Game starting nod for Walker, who will be playing at his home arena. The starters were announced tonight by TNT during the TNT NBA Tip-Off presented by Autotrader pregame show. TNT will unveil the reserves (seven players from each conference), as selected by NBA head coaches, on Thursday, Jan. 31 during TNT NBA Tip-Off at 7 p.m. ET. By virtue of being the top overall finisher in fan voting, James will make the first pick in the First Round (Starters) during the NBA All-Star Draft. Antetokounmpo will have the first pick in the Second Round (Reserves). After the first pick in a round, picks will alternate until all players in that round have been selected. 2019 NBA All-Star Game Starter Pool Stephen Curry, Warriors (6th All-Star selection) Curry has extended his team record for consecutive All-Star Game starting honors to six. Kevin Durant, Warriors (10th All-Star selection) The 2012 Kia NBA All-Star MVP is an All-Star for the 10th season in a row and a starter for the eighth time. Paul George, Thunder (6th All-Star selection) The last time George started the All-Star Game, he made a record nine three-pointers and scored 41 points in 2016. James Harden, Rockets (7th All-Star selection) The Kia NBA MVP for the 2017-18 season has been an All-Star in each of his seven seasons with Houston, putting him third behind Hakeem Olajuwon (12) and Yao Ming (eight) for the most selections in franchise history. LeBron James, Lakers (15th All-Star selection) With three NBA All-Star MVP awards, the career All-Star scoring leader (343 points) is one shy of the record shared by Bryant and Bob Pettit. Giannis Antetokounmpo, Bucks (3rd All-Star selection) Antetokounmpo, who finished second in fan voting among all NBA players for the second year in a row, has been named a starter for the third consecutive season. Joel Embiid, 76ers (2nd All-Star selection) A starter for the second straight year, Embiid scored 19 points for Team Curry in his All-Star Game debut last season. Kyrie Irving, Celtics (6th All-Star selection) An All-Star for the sixth time in eight seasons, the 2014 NBA All-Star MVP received the most fan votes among Eastern Conference guards for the third year in a row. Kawhi Leonard, Raptors (3rd All-Star selection) Voted to start for the third time, Leonard gives Toronto an All-Star Game starter for the fifth consecutive year. Kemba Walker, Hornets (3rd All-Star selection) With his third straight All-Star nod, Walker joins Glen Rice (1996-98) as the only players in Charlotte team history to make at least three All-Star teams. Fans accounted for 50 percent of the vote to determine the NBA All-Star Game starters, while current NBA players and a media panel accounted for 25 percent each. James (4,620,809 fan votes) and Antetokounmpo (4,375,747 fan votes) led their respective conferences and position groups in fan voting. Irving (3,881,766 fan votes) and Curry (3,861,038 fan votes) also topped their respective position groups in fan voting. After all votes were tallied , players were ranked in each conference by position (guard and frontcourt) within each of the three voting groups \u2013 fan votes, player votes and media votes. Each player\u2019s score was calculated by averaging his weighted rank from the fan votes, the player votes and the media votes. The two guards and three frontcourt players with the best score in each conference were named NBA All-Star Game starters. Fan votes served as the tiebreaker for players in a position group with the same score. George won the tiebreaker with the New Orleans Pelicans\u2019 Anthony Davis for the third starting spot in the Western Conference frontcourt group. Below are the overall scores \u2013 based on results from all three voting groups \u2013 for the top finishers at each position. Each player\u2019s score is weighted based on 50 percent for fan vote, 25 percent for player vote and 25 percent for media vote. The formula to determine a player\u2019s score is (Fan Rank * 2 + Player Rank + Media Rank)\/4. "},{"id":36157,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/one-team-one-stat-warriors-jump-shooting-more-ever","date":"2019-01-24","title":"One Team, One Stat: Warriors jump shooting more than ever","content":" * Tonight on TNT:  Warriors vs. Wizards, 8 ET The Golden State Warriors have begun to hit their stride. After what was a seemingly sluggish first half of the season, the Warriors have won eight straight games and sit in first place in the Western Conference . A win in Washington on Thursday would give them the league\u2019s longest winning streak this season. The Warriors have yet to really turn it up defensively. They rank 14th on that end of the floor overall (having allowed a league-average 109.9 points per 100 possessions) and 19th in January (111.2), even with the eight-game winning streak. But the Golden State offense has been better than ever. The Warriors have scored an incredible 126.7 points per 100 possessions over their last 10 games , the best stretch of offense they\u2019ve had in five seasons under coach Steve Kerr. (Prior to this season, their 10-game high was 122.2 points scored per 100 possessions.) Here\u2019s one number to know about the 2018-19 Warriors as they look to extend their winning streak \u2026 The Warriors have taken 61 percent of their shots from outside the paint. That is the highest rate in the league. Four years ago, Charles Barkley said \u2014 in reference to the Warriors \u2014 that a jump-shooting team couldn\u2019t win a championship. He was wrong, of course . He was wrong about the Warriors being that much of a jump-shooting team, first of all. In the 2014-15 season, the Warriors took only 54 percent of their shots from outside the paint. That was the 13th-highest rate in what turned out to be this core\u2019s first championship season. The Warriors were obviously a great shooting team, but they also leveraged their shooting to get layups and dunks. Only one team averaged more points per game in the restricted area than the Warriors that season, when the real jump-shooting team was the LA Clippers, who took 62 percent of their shots from outside the paint. But every season since, the Warriors have gradually become more of a jump-shooting team, seeing an increase in the percentage of their shots that have come from outside the paint. This season, the champs have been outscored by 7.3 points in the paint per game, the league\u2019s third-biggest discrepancy. They\u2019re also in the bottom 10 in regard point differential on free throws (minus-1.5 per game). League-wide, shots in the paint are worth more (1.11 points per attempt) than shots from outside the paint (0.98), even when you take the extra value of 3-pointers into account. Obviously, within those basic boundaries, restricted area shots are worth more than other shots in the paint and 3-pointers are worth more than mid-range shots. But over the last two seasons, the Warriors\u2019 jump shots have also been more likely to come from inside the arc than they were the two seasons prior. The league as a whole has taken 2.2 times as many 3-pointers as mid-range shots this season, up from 1.0 in 2014-15, the first season when the league took more 3-pointers than mid-range shots. The Warriors\u2019 ratio of 3-point attempts to mid-range attempts that season was 1.3, the league\u2019s sixth-highest mark. It climbed to 1.9 (second) the following season and stayed relatively high (1.8 \u2013 seventh highest) in 2016-17, Kevin Durant\u2019s first season with the team. But it dropped last season and the Warriors\u2019 ratio of 1.5 this season is the fourth-lowest in the league. While other teams are extremely disciplined about not taking long 2-point shots (to the point of penalizing players for taking them in scrimmages), the Warriors launch from mid-range without hesitation. Only the Spurs, led by mid-range monsters LaMarcus Aldridge and DeMar DeRozan, have attempted more mid-range shots than the Warriors , who have taken about five times as many mid-range shots as the Houston Rockets. Kevin Durant (311) and Klay Thompson (310) are two of 10 players who have attempted more mid-range shots than the Rockets (208) this season. So in regard to having a analytics-friendly shot chart, the Warriors are near the bottom of the league. And it hasn\u2019t mattered. This season, with all the jump shots, the Warriors have scored 115.6 points per 100 possessions . That makes them the most efficient offensive team of the 23 years for which we have play-by-play data. The Warriors rank 11th in turnover rate , a big improvement from last season, when they ranked 25th . But they also rank 25th in free throw rate and 20th in offensive rebounding percentage . They have the best offense we\u2019ve ever seen almost exclusively because they\u2019ve shot so well and have given themselves more opportunities to shoot by not turning the ball over so much. The Warriors rank second in field goal percentage in the paint, first in mid-range field goal percentage and second in 3-point percentage . No other team ranks in the top five in all three. Durant (74.4 percent) and Thompson (72.1 percent) have been two of the league\u2019s best finishers in the restricted area among non-bigs. Stephen Curry ranks third in field goal percentage on non-restricted-area paint shots (minimum 50 FGA). Durant has been the league\u2019s best mid-range shooter . And Curry ranks fifth in 3-point percentage (having attempted a lot more 3-pointers than anyone else in the top 25 ). Both Curry and Thompson have seen an increase in the percentage of their shots that have come from outside the paint since that first championship season. But the biggest change in the Warriors\u2019 shots from four seasons ago has come from their bigs. It\u2019s not about where their bigs\u2019 shots are coming from, but in the number of shots their bigs have been getting. Warriors bigs not named Draymond Green \u2014 Kevon Looney, Jordan Bell, Damian Jones and DeMarcus Cousins \u2014 have attempted just 8.9 shots per game this season, down from 15.4 last season (from the first three guys plus David West, Zaza Pachulia and JaVale McGee) and 18.4 in \u201914-15 (Andrew Bogut, Marreese Speights, etc.). Cousins, of course, has played in just two games thus far. Over his nine seasons in the league, only *six players have scored more points in the paint than Cousins. The percentage of his shots that have come from the paint has **dropped over the last two seasons, and he hasn\u2019t been ***a very good finisher in the restricted area for his size. Still, he gives the Warriors the best paint scorer they\u2019ve had on this five-year run. So, as the season goes on and Cousins plays more minutes, the Warriors should become less of a jump-shooting team. And we\u2019ll see if a more balanced offense (in regard to shot location) is a more efficient one. If so, yikes. It\u2019s not new to me, it\u2019s just been a while. It\u2019s all part of the business.\u201d Gasol expressed frustration Wednesday that Conley was even being included in trade talks. \u201cI don\u2019t understand why Mike is in those talks either,\u201d Gasol said. \u201cMike is one heck of a player, and we\u2019re going to need good players moving forward. I don\u2019t understand why Mike is in this.\u201d Per ESPN\u2019s Adrian Wojnarowski , Gasol and Conley recently met with Pera in Memphis, but neither expressed a desire to be dealt. Memphis began the season well, boasting a 12-5 mark after a road win against the San Antonio Spurs on Nov. 21 \u2014 a victory sealed by a pair of Gasol free throws with 0.7 seconds left. Since then, the Grizzlies have swooned, going 7-23 and falling to 14th in the West . The Grizzlies have lost five straight and are 1-9 in their last 10 games. During the five-game skid, opponents have shot 42 percent from 3-point range and the Grizzlies have allowed 117.6 points per 100 possessions . Memphis hosts the Charlotte Hornets tonight ( 8 ET, NBA League Pass ) to start a five-game home stand that lasts through Jan. 30. Gasol can become a free agent this summer if he opts out of the final year of his current contract. Conley has an early-termination option for 2020-21 and, per ESPN\u2019s Adrian Wojnarowski , has $22.4 million of his $34.5 million salary guaranteed. The balance of the deal will become fully protected once he plays in 55 games (Conley has played in 46 games so far). Conley and Gasol rank No. 1 and No. 2, respectively, in games played for Memphis ( Conley is at 764, Gasol 762 ). They are also either No. 1 or No. 2 in several other all-time Grizzlies categories including points scored (Gasol leads with 11,554), assists (Conley, 4,341), steals (Conley, 1,129), rebounds (Gasol, 5,877) and blocks (Gasol, 1,132). The pair guided Memphis\u2019 greatest era of success, which included seven straight playoff appearances (2010-17) and the franchise\u2019s only appearance in the Western Conference finals (2013) . \u201cWhen I signed back a couple years ago, that\u2019s a thought that goes through your head that, \u2018man, I could play in the same place for 14 or 15 years,\u201d Conley said. \u201cThat\u2019d be awesome, and hopefully retire one day as a Grizzly. You also understand that in three, four years a lot can happen and a lot can change. Memphis is all I know. This is my home. I love everybody here and my teammates and the organization. I don\u2019t know any better. My question for you: Who is Milwaukee\u2019s second star?  * * * Steve Aschburner :  Khris Middleton , like it or not. You can make small-to-medium-sized cases for other Bucks such as Brook Lopez, Eric Bledsoe and Malcolm Brogdon, each valuable in significant ways to the ensemble. But Middleton is the shooter, scorer and defender to best complement Giannis Antetokounmpo, a potential full-service sidekick \u2026 who has disappeared at an alarming rate through the first half of 2018-19. Being able to bring it every night in support of the team\u2019s Kia MVP candidate is vital, especially given Milwaukee\u2019s salary-cap limitations. I can\u2019t see GM Jon Horst snagging an alternative No. 2 in the next couple weeks. So it\u2019s on Middleton to demonstrate his true worth from now through springtime. Harden\u2019s run of 30-point performances now trails only NBA legend Wilt Chamberlain, who posted runs of 20, 25, 31 and 65 games at various points from 1960-62. In an interview with Jonathan Feigen of the Houston Chronicle , Harden says as great as his scoring feat has been, he\u2019s ultimately driven to be mentioned among the game\u2019s all-time greats . \u201cKobe [Bryant] and Wilt and [Michael] Jordan \u2014 now we\u2019re talking about the elites of the game, the greatest to ever touch a basketball,\u201d Harden told the newspaper . \u201cIt\u2019s honorable to be up there with those names. Honest, I have a long way to go. I\u2019m not even close to what they accomplished in their careers. But it\u2019s pretty cool to be in that conversation and almost there. But I have a lot of work to do. \u201cThat\u2019s one of the reasons you play the game of basketball: to be, when it\u2019s all said and done, mentioned as one of the greats, the greatest that ever dribbled a basketball, whether it\u2019s Wilt, whether it\u2019s Jordan, and the list goes on. Obviously, you want to win championships and want the individual accomplishments, but every day (when) I\u2019m in the gym and work on moves, I think about that. \u201cWhen I\u2019m done, whenever that is, I want my name up there with them. It\u2019s a good place to be in.\u201d Harden\u2019s scoring run began on Dec. 13, in a 126-121 win against the L.A. Lakers . Since then, Houston has gone 13-6 and moved to No. 5 in the West . That average would be the NBA\u2019s highest since Jordan led the league in scoring with 37.1 ppg in 1986-87 . If he maintains this pace, Harden\u2019s average would be the ninth-highest single-season scoring average in league history. Here\u2019s more from Wojnarowski on Anthony\u2019s next steps: In the summer of 2014 , the Bulls tried to woo Anthony \u2014 then a top-level free agent \u2014 to Chicago. Two giant digital images above the entrance on Madison Street showed Anthony in a Bulls No. 7 jersey dribbling next to a championship trophy. Anthony arrived at a decked-out United Center on the afternoon of July 1, 2014 with agent Leon Rose and coach Tom Thibodeau, a police SUV trailing their oversized limousine. However, a move to Chicago never happened as Anthony opted to re-sign with the New York Knicks , his team at the time. Anthony and the Rockets agreed to part ways in mid-November after the team\u2019s slow start to the season. The 10-time All-Star played just 10 games for Houston after signing a one-year, $2.4 million deal during the offseason. Anthony was traded from the Oklahoma City Thunder to the Atlanta Hawks last July before the Hawks released him to clear the way for him to sign with the Rockets. Houston thought he could be the piece it needed to finally get past Golden State and win its first championship since back-to-back titles in 1994-95. Instead the Rockets limped out to a 6-7 start and the emergence of undrafted rookie Gary Clark made it appear that Anthony would have to take a reduced role. In the end the Rockets decided it would be better to move on than to force Anthony to do that. \u201cWe just had to see how things worked out,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said at the time . \u201cAnd the way we play probably wasn\u2019t conducive to his game and he was trying to make the necessary sacrifices and it wasn\u2019t fair to him as a Hall of Fame player to play in a way that wasn\u2019t good for him, wasn\u2019t good for us. It just wasn\u2019t a fit.\u201d The 34-year-old Anthony has had a tough time over the last two seasons. He averaged a career-low 16.2 points in 78 starts in a tumultuous season for the Thunder last season before coming to Houston \u2014 and accepting a reserve role for the first time in his 16-year career. Eight of Anthony\u2019s 10 appearances for the Rockets came off the bench after he had started all 1,054 games he\u2019d played in his first 15 NBA seasons. D\u2019Antoni said he feels for Anthony that things ended this way and made it clear that it wasn\u2019t a matter of Anthony not having the right attitude in Houston. \u201cIn the summer we tried to hit a home run and it didn\u2019t work out,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cHe tried everything he could. He was great while he was here. It just didn\u2019t work out for whatever reason. I just thank him for his professionalism. It was good. He tried everything he could to make it work and it just didn\u2019t work out.\u201d The third overall pick in the 2003 draft has averaged 24 points, 6.5 rebounds and 3 assists in a career that also included stints with the Denver Nuggets and the New York Knicks. Anthony sat out Houston\u2019s last three games with what the team called an illness. His last appearance for Houston came in a blowout loss to Oklahoma City on Nov. 8 when he had two points and five rebounds. The 10th overall pick in the 2010 Draft, George started his career in Indiana, helping the Pacers to back-to-back trips to the Eastern Conference finals , where he shined on the big stage against Miami\u2019s \u201cBig 3\u201d Heat squad led by LeBron James, Dwyane Wade and Chris Bosh. But a devastating injury , a trade demand and wild, free-agent summer that-never-was later, led him to his current situation as one of the faces of the Oklahoma City Thunder. George and Russell Westbrook are the leaders of a Thunder squad that is again a legitimate challenger in the Western Conference \u2013 both now and for the foreseeable future. The timing couldn\u2019t be better for George, the Southern California native who spurned LeBron and the hometown Lakers for an opportunity to find his own lane with the Thunder. Overall, he\u2019s in a great place, on and off the court. One of the league\u2019s top two-way players, George has emerged as a dark horse Kia MVP candidate this season while playing alongside triple-double machine\/2017 Kia MVP Westbrook. His family is comfortable in Oklahoma City, the midwestern city that embraced the Georges at what turned out to be the perfect time. George spoke to NBA.com \u2018s Sekou Smith about all that and more. * * * Sekou Smith:  You\u2019ve been a great player in this league for a long time, played in two Eastern Conference finals and competed against the best at the highest levels. But I\u2019ve never seen you as good on both ends as you\u2019ve been this season. Do you feel like your game has ascended to another level? Paul George:  Yeah, yeah. Definitely. I think you just get a feel, an understanding of the game that leads to where I am now. I know my pace, I know my game and what\u2019s comfortable for me. And at this point in my career, I\u2019ve seen every defense you can see. There\u2019s nothing you can throw at me that I haven\u2019t already seen, mentally or physically. And defensively I know every angle. I mean \u2026 I do my homework. I know what guys like to do, I know tendencies. I just know what an average basketball player would do in certain moments, and I just play to that. SS:  It\u2019s almost like you\u2019ve solved the matrix or something. PG:  It just feels honestly, man, like everything has slowed down at this stage of my career. All the years I\u2019ve been in this league, it\u2019s like \u2026 say a kid is being taught algebra. And he\u2019s got all of these math problems going on. And everything, I\u2019m just pulling from it and grabbing it and I can see through concepts and understand what\u2019s going on out there. It\u2019s a fun way to play, when there aren\u2019t any crazy surprises that anyone can throw at you. SS:  I know when you come into this league, everybody is working to get there. Everybody wants to be on that list of truly elite players in this game. Does it feel different when you actually get there after all the years of hard work? And how do you know when you\u2019ve gotten there? Is it a certain way teams deal with you, a respect level for you, that shows up when you get there? PG:  It does, especially in the way other teams deal with you and come at you. I think the notion now is to \u201cbe physical and get into him.\u201d And then a lot of times it\u2019s like an emphasis to try and take me out of the game early, which again, I\u2019ve seen every way I can be guarded. So it almost helps, in a way, for teams to start the game off aggressively coming at me and trying to trap me. That plays into my game. I like to play myself into a game. I\u2019m never going to come out shooting, trying to get mine or anything like that. I like to let the game come to me and set guys up. And then I can pick and choose when I can be aggressive, when I need to be aggressive. So when teams play like that, when they are deliberate about trying to take me out of the game, they\u2019re just playing into my hands. SS:  Are you as comfortable off the court now as you are on the court? You\u2019re not the young buck anymore. You\u2019re all grown up now, settled in Oklahoma City with your family and everything else seemingly in place. P G:  Listen, life has been good. I\u2019ve got two little ones and a beautiful woman at home. I\u2019m close with my teammates here. I\u2019m at peace, honestly. I\u2019m at peace. All I have to do is go out there and play. I don\u2019t have to worry about trade rumors or things like that. I don\u2019t have to worry about contract extensions or how things are going to work out. Everything is set in stone right now and I\u2019m really comfortable, in the best way possible. I\u2019m relaxed in that part of my life. SS:  Based on the conversations you and Russ(ell Westbrook) had in the offseason, do you think this team is where you expected it to be a little past the midway point of the season? PG:  Yeah, I definitely think so. With that being said, though, I think there is a lot of room for improvement for us. We knew where we wanted to be coming back off of last season. And we\u2019re in that neighborhood. We wanted to be one of the best teams in the West. SS:  I know it started slow \u2026 PG:  It did, it started slow. But that\u2019s expected when you consider what we were coming from last season. We started without Russ and we had to learn to play without Russ. I had to carry a little extra weight in trying to get us going offensively and defensively. And we played without countless numbers of guys being out of the rotation who play a lot of minutes for us. It was a little bit all over the place to start the season. But I think still, we\u2019re right where we need to be. SS:  For years the Western Conference had its own hierarchy in terms of which teams fit where in the playoff picture. It feels a little different now with all these upstart teams challenging for playoff spots. Even with the Warriors, seeming as vulnerable as they\u2019ve been in years, it feels different now. Is the chase different now as well? PG:  It\u2019s still Golden State as the team to beat, regardless if they are No. 1 in the standings or wherever they are seeded at. They\u2019re still the team we have to go through, that everybody has to go through in the West. We just wanted to be seeded well come playoff time. That\u2019s when we have to be at our best. And that\u2019s the team we have to be gunning for. SS:  Does the evolution of some of these younger guys on the roster, coupled with the veteran stars already established, make you feel better about the pursuit, whatever it is and wherever it ends, this season? PG:  Let me say this: I think Steven Adams is one of the best players at his position, and he doesn\u2019t get a lot of credit for what he does. Terrance Ferguson is one of the young promising defenders and 3-point shooters in our league. And he has so much room where he can take his game to. I just wanted to point that out. And look, we rely on so many young guys, outside of myself, Russ, Ray (Felton) and a couple of our other vets, we lean on a group of guys who are basically three or four years and younger into their NBA careers. Even Jerami Grant, who has been great for us, is still a young guy. He\u2019s just 24. But he\u2019s been huge, the X-factor really. His ability to switch on defense, run the floor, play above the rim and then stretch the floor, as just been huge for us. And he\u2019s still young. But I think that\u2019s a good thing, that we really, really count on our young guys to help us get to where we are right now. SS:  That brings up a great point about where this team and really this franchise sits right now, in terms of the foundation. There aren\u2019t many teams fortified at all levels, at so many positions, and with stars and role players and everything else in between. Does is it seem a little crazy in this league how things can seem so shaky one minute and then so solid the next? PG:  It does. It really does. It\u2019s clear [GM] Sam [Presti] and our front office guys have done a hell of a job. And I can only think of how good we can be, especially defensively, once Andre Roberson is back in the rotation and the lift he\u2019ll give us. We\u2019re already one of the best defensive teams in the league and now we\u2019re talking about adding one of the best individual defenders in the game back into the mix and our starting lineup. You just never know where we could be when it all comes together this season and into the future. You never know who\u2019s going to want to come and join me and Russ and the rest of these guys on this journey. But I feel comfortable saying that we\u2019re solid right now and in a really good spot. * * * Sekou Smith is a veteran NBA reporter and NBA TV analyst. Johnson, who played in 524 career games with Milwaukee over seven seasons from 1977-84, will become the ninth player in Bucks history to have his number retired. \u201cThis is a well-deserved honor for Marques who was a pillar of one of the most successful eras of Bucks basketball in the late 1970s and 1980s,\u201d said Bucks and Fiserv Forum President Peter Feigin. \u201cMarques is one of the most decorated players in franchise history and played a large role on some of the winningest teams in the Bucks\u2019 51 seasons. Retiring Marques\u2019 number was an easy decision for us. We look forward to recognizing his prolific career on March 24.\u201d \u201cI am moved beyond words by such a gesture,\u201d Johnson said. \u201cI have always held a special place in my heart for the fans who supported the Bucks during my time there. For the organization to honor me this way, means more than words can express. Sometimes it takes being away from a situation to really appreciate what you had. I had long felt a sense of disappointment for falling short of the NBA Finals. What I have come to realize is that the fans of Milwaukee only ask that you play hard and give your best.\u201d Part of one of the most dominating eras of Bucks basketball, Johnson, a four-time All-Star and three-time All-NBA honoree with the Bucks, led Milwaukee to a 347-227 (.605) regular season record and playoff appearances in six of his seven seasons with the team. This included five straight playoff appearances from 1980-84, two Eastern Conference Finals berths in 1983 and 1984 and four consecutive 50-win seasons from 1980-84. Johnson averaged 21.0 points (fourth-highest in team history), 7.5 rebounds and 3.7 assists per game and shot 53.0 percent from the field (fourth-highest in team history) in his time with the Bucks. He ranks among the franchise\u2019s all-time leaders in nearly every statistical category including being sixth in points (10,980), fourth in field goals made (4,546), third in rebounds (3,923), first in offensive rebounds (1,468) and ninth in games played (524). He averaged more than 20.0 points in five seasons and was named to the 1977-78 All-NBA Rookie Team after averaging 19.5 points and 10.6 rebounds per game. Johnson was also a First Team All-NBA pick for the 1978-79 season and a Second Team All-NBA selection after the 1979-80 and 1980-81 seasons. Originally selected by the Bucks with the third overall pick in the 1977 NBA Draft out of UCLA, Johnson won the 1975 NCAA Championship with the Bruins under legendary head coach John Wooden. He was also named the Associated Press and Naismith Men\u2019s College Player of the Year, and won the first-ever John R. Wooden Award following his senior season in 1976-77 in which he averaged 21.4 points and 11.1 rebounds per game. UCLA retired Johnson\u2019s No. 54 in 1996. Currently an Emmy-Award-Winning analyst for Bucks broadcasts on FOX Sports Wisconsin, Johnson is a nominee for the Naismith Basketball Hall of Fame, a member of the College Basketball Hall of Fame and will be inducted into the Wisconsin Sports Hall of Fame on Thursday. Johnson\u2019s No. 8 will hang from the Fiserv Forum rafters alongside Oscar Robertson (No. 1), Junior Bridgeman (No. 2), Sidney Moncrief (No. 4), Bob Dandridge (No. 10), Jon McGlocklin (No. 14), Bob Lanier (No. 16), Brian Winters (No. 32) and Kareem Abdul-Jabbar (No. 33)."},{"id":36208,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/pelicans-anthony-davis-sidelined-1-2-weeks","date":"2019-01-19","title":"Pelicans' Davis expected to miss 1-2 weeks with finger injury","content":" NEW ORLEANS (AP) \u2014 The New Orleans Pelicans say Anthony Davis has a sprained finger that is expected to sideline him up to two weeks . So was that of Festus Ezeli, of JaVale McGee, of Anderson Varejao, of Andrew Bogut, of Jordan Bell and, of course, the Zaza. Who will ever forget the Zaza? They were all fine men and devoted teammates who suited up every night at center and did whatever the Golden State Warriors asked of them, which means not much because the demands weren\u2019t, shall we say, steep, or extending beyond what their skills were capable of offering. For the first time since the Warriors began collecting jewelry, they have a body in the middle who could put the other team, and certainly all the referees, on notice almost every night. On Friday, DeMarcus Cousins officially brought his four All-Star honors along with a surgically-repaired Achilles\u2019 tendon to the mix against the Clippers. And the two-time defending champs \u2014 certainly not deprived of talent \u2014 are nonetheless hoping their title chances in the Cousins Era will mirror his first basket of the season: A slam dunk. Cousins made a grand entrance that was 11 months in the planning, roughly the duration of his rehabilitation. Set up perfectly by Kevin Durant on the pick-and-roll just 90 seconds into the game, Cousins took a bounce pass and shook the rim, punctuating the dunk with a satisfying scream and a stinkface for effect. \u201cJust glad to know I can still dunk,\u201d he said. \u201cIt felt good. Never in a million years would I have thought a dunk would be my first basket coming back.\u201d You can understand the outbreak of pent-up emotion. When Cousins fell hard to the floor last January, he was a member of the Pelicans and prepping for a big free agent payday that summer. Sadly, he didn\u2019t get that cash because of the serious injury, and not-so-sadly, he left the Pelicans for the formidable Warriors, who now run out a starting five that have each made multiple trips to the All-Star Game. Cousins is working on the cheap, so to speak, this season, yet has drastically increased his odds of cashing in on his first title by playing alongside Durant, Stephen Curry, Klay Thompson and Draymond Green. One night, encouraging as it was \u2014 14 points, six rebounds and 15 not-so-exhausting minutes \u2014 didn\u2019t unlock all the questions swirling around Cousins and his body and how he\u2019ll fit with his decorated teammates and the uptempo style they often play. For the time being, it\u2019ll do . \u201cI felt like a kid on Christmas,\u201d he said. \u201cIt\u2019s been a long journey. It was one of the best days of my life being on the floor again playing the game I love. My teammates supported me this entire process. Made it easy as possible for me. They understood my struggle.\u201d Cousins, at age 28, should still be in the prime stage of a solid career \u2014 a center with a collection of offensive skills that set him apart from his peers. Yet he knows all too well about the history of players recovering from such a debilitating injury; only Dominique Wilkins bounced back to All-Star form. Plus, Cousins is a big man carrying a listed 270 pounds. That\u2019s not an obvious recipe for continued of success. With the Warriors, there\u2019s no urgency from a basketball perspective. Golden State won three titles without him and, with him, are heavily favored to add a fourth. He\u2019s a bonus, an insurance policy, or perhaps even a final piece to another celebratory result come June. Between now and then, the Warriors and Cousins will go about the business of searching for a tailored fit. It\u2019s something that coach Steve Kerr says will be a challenge, though a pleasant one, he suspects. \u201cWe\u2019ve got to figure out how all that works with rotations and substitution patterns and ease him back,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cWe\u2019ve already had discussions as a staff and team. We\u2019re just trying to win. That means players have to accept roles and accept that some nights it\u2019s their nights and other nights it\u2019s someone else\u2019s night. As long as we\u2019re in step as a team \u2014 and we\u2019ve established that over the years.\u201d There\u2019s another element at work here: Cousins is playing for money this summer as a free agent. He was in line for a nine-figure payday before his injury, but didn\u2019t receive any offers after, which led him to the Warriors on a one-year deal. Cousins figured if he couldn\u2019t cash in right away, he might as well play for a more economical wage with the league\u2019s best team. Will Cousins put aside personal goals and accept lesser touches for the good of the Warriors and the championship chase? On this team, he might not even be the third option. In that sense, Kerr doesn\u2019t want Cousins to feel any outward pressure to be his pre-injury self right away. \u201cIt\u2019s been a year since his injury but this is almost like training camp,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cThe game is going to be moving fast. He\u2019s got to get his legs, feel comfortable with his new teammates. These things take time. I think that\u2019s the biggest message. This is not the end of the story, it\u2019s the middle of the story. It\u2019s a milestone and there\u2019s a long way to go.\u201d By all accounts, Cousins has the support of the locker room. NBA players are a fraternity and in this case, they know Cousins missed out on riches. They realize the sacrifice he\u2019s making -\u2014 or was forced to make -\u2014 and sympathize. That much was evident a split-second after Cousins\u2019 dunk; the entire Warriors\u2019 bench went airborne in celebration. And after Cousins fouled out, he walked to a bench full of teammates who smothered him with a standing ovation and high fives. He chuckled at that. \u201cProbably the fakest love I ever seen,\u201d he said, laughing. The first game presented the full Cousins experience: Good shots, a few solid plays, and arguing over foul calls. If this is any indication, Cousins will be hard to miss on the floor, even among All-Star teammates And he appears at ease with the Warriors. Over several years, he developed a reputation as a sulking, moody and temperamental star with a Kings franchise that never made the playoffs with him. Part of it was immaturity, which led to suspensions, and part due to the misery of the Kings, who drafted poorly and failed in almost every effort to give Cousins help. He went to a better place after being traded to the Pelicans two Februarys ago, but the injury prevented him from gaining any traction with the Pelicans. With the Warriors and ample talent around him, Cousins feels totally unburdened from expectations. It\u2019s not too unlike his stint with Team USA, in that both the Olympians and the Warriors are embarrassment of riches. Cousins, for instance, was caught off-guard by the lack of defenders thrown his way Friday by the Clippers, who couldn\u2019t afford to leave Thompson or Durant or Curry open. \u201cThis is a first,\u201d Cousins said. \u201cI definitely can get used to this.\u201d There were the expected moments when he stumbled with the ball and was out of sync on the floor. Cousins chalked most of it up to nerves, but also his lack of preparation with the team. \u201cEvery time I touched the ball I felt like I was going to travel, going to trip over my feet,\u201d he said. \u201cI just had to take my time with my decisions. And then I was feeling my rhythm.\u201d He hit three of his four 3-pointers, which shows how easily he can fit right in with the long-ball Warriors if that continues. That\u2019s they lacked in the starting centers who came before him. None were remotely this offensively gifted. \u201cI like that he\u2019s going to keep people honest at the three-point line,\u201d said Durant. \u201cHe was running the floor, setting screens, just playing his game. In 15 minutes, he had 14 points and six rebounds so turn that to 25 minutes, that\u2019s an easy 20 and 10. I like where he\u2019s going. It was a good first step and hopefully he keeps moving forward.\u201d Of course, the next game might not be as friendly for Cousins. Comebacks can turn drastically without much warning; such is the unpredictability of the body and timing and dealing with a new situation. \u201cWe\u2019re all just trying to reassure him that it\u2019s not just about tonight,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cThere will be a lot of criticism and judgments and maybe compliments. He\u2019s going to get a lot of love, or a lot of \u2018Is this a fit?\u2019 One of good things about him being here the first few months, he\u2019s got an up close look at the world we live in, where when we lose a game it\u2019s the end of the world to a lot of people. He\u2019s felt that and he knows the spotlight\u2019s going to be on him, good or bad, and he\u2019s got to take it for what it is.\u201d Said Cousins: \u201cYou get judged by your every moment. As long as the guys in the room know what the situation is and ultimate goal, that\u2019s all that matters.\u201d And then he said something else, something that could send chills around a league that\u2019s already fretting over the Warriors: \u201cWe can get a whole lot better. * * * Shaun Powell has covered the NBA for more than 25 years. Reigning Kia MVP James Harden knows that better than most, given his checkered recent history with the NBA\u2019s top individual regular-season honor. Harden believed his case to be rock-solid in two separate seasons , but came up short both times before finally breaking through last season. Sure, his numbers were off the charts in 2016-17 , when he finished second to his friend (and former Oklahoma City Thunder teammate) Russell Westbrook. The same goes for 2014-15 , when he finished second to Golden State Warriors superstar Stephen Curry in the first year of Curry\u2019s back-to-back seasons winning the award . Harden did win the NBPA\u2019s first MVP in a vote of his peers, but the sting of losing out to Curry was already there. The place where Harden came up short in both instances was in the narrative department, which, like it or not, has always been a crucial component for the media-panel voters. Westbrook\u2019s campaign came both during his historic (first) triple-double season and immediately after 2014 Kia MVP Kevin Durant bolted for the Warriors in free agency. Curry\u2019s first win was on the strength of his (and the Warriors\u2019 breakout season) that ended a 40-year title drought . His second MVP came as he fueled the Warriors\u2019 record-breaking 73-win season . Truth be told, a large part of Harden\u2019s compelling narrative last season was his previous near-misses (not to mention the Rockets\u2019 wire-to-wire run as the NBA\u2019s best team and their league-best 66 wins ). With the winds changing seemingly by the day in this season\u2019s MVP chase \u2014 thanks to the work Harden and Milwaukee\u2019s Giannis Antetokounmpo are treating fans to \u2014 Harden is crafting yet another gripping drama for voters to consider. Dragging the Rockets from 14th place in the Western Conference standings last month to their current fifth-place perch is a great place to start. Doing it with Chris Paul and other rotation players injured fed the drama. And chasing history \u2014 18 straight games of scoring 30 or more points in a run the league hasn\u2019t seen since Wilt Chamberlain\u2019s days \u2014 always punches up the script. \u201cAll you need is eyeballs to know what\u2019s going on. James has been unbelievable and what he\u2019s done for that team is unreal,\u201d a Western Conference executive said. \u201cThe hard sell this season is in what these guys are doing on the court, both he and Giannis. There really isn\u2019t a need to create some back story for any of these guys, and I include Steph in that as well. He\u2019s on that level, too. There\u2019s plenty of season left, though, for all of these guys. It\u2019s too early to make any final declarations, isn\u2019t it?\u201d Indeed. There is much more season to play out, for the current frontrunners and everyone else. But as they all know, it\u2019s never too soon to start weaving that narrative that might push your campaign over the top. * * * The top five this week in the 2018-19 Kia Race to the MVP Ladder: * * * Last week:  No. 2 Season stats :  35.4 points, 8.5 assists, 6.3 rebounds, 2.0 steals His quest for a back-to-back Kia MVPs is a very real possibility, given Harden\u2019s current performance. He\u2019s on a nuclear run, averaging 40 points per game over his past 20 and scored at least 30 points in 18 straight games , which is the longest streak since the ABA\/NBA merger. He is averaging a bonkers 47.6 points, 9.8 rebounds, 7.6 assists and 2.6 steals in his past five games. His back-to-back games of 58 and 57 points mark the NBA\u2019s first back-to-back 50s since he did it on Dec. 20 and 22 of 2017 . The last time a player posted back-to-back games with 55 or more points was Wilt Chamberlain on Dec. 11 and 14 of 1962 . Harden\u2019s work rate is at an all-time high these days because so much of his usual supporting cast is wounded and\/or unavailable. Chris Paul is still out . Center Clint Capela could miss anywhere from four to six weeks after thumb surgery . If Harden keeps the Rockets in the mix through all of this, it would be hard for anyone to argue against him keeping that MVP trophy he so adores. He pounded the Hawks for 33 points in 31 minutes in Sunday\u2019s win in Atlanta. That\u2019s a good thing for \u201cThe Greek Freak,\u201d whether he realizes it or not. Because the load he\u2019ll be asked to carry in the 2019 playoffs trumps anything that\u2019s been asked of him in the past. These Bucks will enter the playoffs with high expectations and Budenholzer will need their catalyst at his healthy best down the stretch of this season. Antetokoumpo must steal moments for a rest wherever he can get them now. After roasting the New Orleans Pelicans for 41 points and nine 3-pointers Wednesday , Curry became the first player in NBA history to make eight or more 3-pointers in three straight games . To open 2019, Curry has three 40-point games while averaging 34.1 points (on 50.6 percent shooting and 47.7 percent on 3-pointers), 6.0 assists, 5.3 rebounds and 1.7 steals. That continued Leonard\u2019s season-long trend of not playing on the second night of back-to-back sets. But working without one of the league\u2019s elite two-way players is something Raptors coach Nick Nurse can live with now because he knows he won\u2019t have to do so come playoff time. In fact, preserving Leonard at this time makes sense for a team with designs on a playoff run they hope stretches into June and, thus, The Finals. He\u2019s shown himself to be every bit the difference-maker Raptors boss Masai Ujiri hoped he\u2019d be when he shook the franchise up last summer in trading for him. Kanter said he feared he could be attacked or killed over his opposition to Turkey President Recep Tayyip Erdogan if he were to travel to London. Istanbul-based newspaper Daily Sabah reported that an arrest warrant was issued for Kanter by Turkish prosecutors on Wednesday. Silver said NBA officials never suggested that Kanter skip the game but understand why he chose not to travel. \u201cThere are significant issues that he is dealing with, and I recognize that for the NBA, by virtue of the fact that we\u2019re a global business, we have to pay a lot of attention to those issues as well,\u201d Silver said. \u201cI will say there\u2019s nothing more important to me, as the commissioner of the league, the safety and security of our players, and so we take very seriously the threats that he has received, (even if) it\u2019s just people on social media. \u201cAgain, I support Enes, a player in this league, and I support the platform that our players have to speak out on issues that are important to them.\u201d The Daily Sabah reported that Turkish prosecutors are seeking an Interpol \u201cred notice,\u201d which is an international request for arrest and extradition, for Kanter, who was accused of membership in a terror organization. He was said to have provided financial support to exiled Muslim cleric Fethullah Gulen, who has been blamed by the Turkish government as being responsible for a failed coup in Turkey in 2016. The Associated Press has been unable to independently verify those reports. Kanter said Wednesday on Twitter that the Turkish government could not present \u201cany single piece of evidence of my wrongdoing\u201d and that he doesn\u2019t \u201ceven have a parking ticket in the U.S.\u201d Kanter, who has frequently criticized Erdogan, has had his Turkish passport revoked. He noted in an op-ed he wrote for The Washington Post earlier this week that he does not yet have U.S. citizenship or a U.S. passport \u2013 either of which would offer him greater legal protection. He learned of the cancellation of his Turkish passport on May 20, 2017, when he was detained in Bucharest, Romania, upon returning from a trip to Indonesia to run a basketball camp for his charitable foundation. He was later granted safe passage to London before returning to the United States. Turkey has insisted on numerous occasions that its detention of academics and activists for allegedly supporting anti-government protests, which have intensified following the failed coup, are an important part of its fight against extremist groups. \u201cErdogan is doing whatever he can, such as using institutions like the Interpol to execute his brutal international policy of persecution against his critics, including abductions and kidnappings of innocent Turkish people living abroad,\u201d Celine Assaf Boustani, an international lawyer at the Human Rights Foundation, told The Associated Press. \u201cInterpol should reject Turkey\u2019s request to issue a red notice arrest warrant for Kanter and uphold its constitution, which strictly forbids Interpol to undertake any politically motivated intervention or activity.\u201d Kanter, who had played in every Knicks game this season until missing the last two with an illness, is averaging 14.4 points and a team-high 11 rebounds. Devin Booker (PHO) 405,432 * * * After all votes are tallied, players will be ranked in each conference by position (guard and frontcourt) within each of the three voting groups \u2013 fan votes, player votes and media votes. Each player\u2019s score will be calculated by averaging his weighted rank from the fan votes, the player votes and the media votes. The two guards and three frontcourt players with the best score in each conference will be named NBA All-Star Game starters. Fan voting will serve as the tiebreaker for players in a position group with the same score. NBA All-Star Voting 2019 presented by Google runs from Dec. 25 \u2013 Jan. 21.
